                        <article class="article clearfix">
                            <!-- Start Silva content --> 
<h1 class="heading">MA/MSc in Digital Humanities</h1>
<p class="lead">The Master's degree in
Digital Humanities at UCL draws together teaching from a wide range
of disciplines, to investigate the application of computational
technologies to the arts, humanities, and cultural heritage. </p>
<p class="p"> The MA/MSc in Digital
Humanities is a truly interdisciplinary programme and has strong teaching links with: </p>
<ul class="disc">
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis" target="_self">UCL Department of Information Studies</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/" target="_self">UCL
Computer Science</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/ah/" target="_self">Arts and Humanities</a></li>
<li> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/shs/" target="_self">Social and Historical
Sciences</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/engineering/" target="_self">Engineering Science</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.bartlett.ucl.ac.uk/index.php" target="_self">Bartlett Faculty of the Built
Environment</a>. </li>
</ul>
<p class="p">       The programme also draws on facilities offered by:</p>
<ul class="disc">
<li> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/library/" target="_self">UCL Library Services</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/library/special-coll/" target="_self">Special Collections</a></li>
<li><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/museums/" target="_self">UCL Museums
and Collections</a></li>
</ul>
<p class="p">       as well as liaising closely with a variety of
world-class, London based libraries, archives, and museums within the
vicinity of UCL.</p>

<h2 class="heading">About the Programme</h2>





<p class="p">      The MA/MSc provides research-led teaching delivered by leading scholars.</p>
<p class="p">                  In
Term 1 and 2, students take five core modules, plus a further
three from a wide range of options available from various departments and
faculties at UCL. In addition, students write an original <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony/dissertations" target="_blank">dissertation</a> on a topic of their choice in consultation with their supervisor,
and undertake a <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony/workplacements" target="_blank">workplacement</a> at a related institution where they can apply
taught aspects of the programme in Term 3. This allows students who have a
background in the humanities to acquire necessarily skills in digital
technologies, and also makes it possible for those with a technical
background to become informed about scholarly methods in the humanities.</p>

<h2 class="heading">Terms One and Two</h2>





<p class="p"> The following core modules are mandatory for the programme:</p>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG008" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG008" target="_self">Digital Resources in the Humanities</a><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG008" target="_self"></a> </dt>
  <dd><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG008" target="_blank"></a>Introducing a range of
issues involved in the design, creation, management and use of
digital resources in the humanities. 
</dd>
</dl>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG017" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG017" target="_self">Internet
Technologies</a><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG017" target="_self"></a> </dt>
  <dd>Exploring the basic concepts of markup, website structuring and design, and issues involved in generating, evaluating and delivering online content. 
</dd>
</dl>
<p class="p"> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG017" target="_blank"></a></p>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank">Introduction to Programming and Scripting</a> </dt>
  <dd><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank"></a>      Providing an introduction to the key concepts and 
principles of standard procedural computer programming and a brief 
introduction to relational database querying and manipulation.</dd>
</dl>
<p class="p"> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank"></a></p>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank">Server Programming and Structured Data</a> </dt>
  <dd><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank"></a>Covering approaches to creating database driven 
websites, with a focus on applications relating to maps and spatial 
data. </dd>
</dl>
<p class="p"> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank"></a></p>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank">XML</a> </dt>
  <dd><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank"></a>Providing an overview
of Extensible Markup language; giving students the opportunity to
practice XML markup techniques, processing with XSLT, and demonstrating the use of XML in
publishing.</dd>
</dl>
<p class="p"> Note that the technical core modules are all at entry level; for 
students that already have demonstrable competencies in these areas, it 
may be possible, subject to the agreement of the Programme Director, to 
substitute modules from other UCL departments.</p>
<p class="p"> There are also a wide range of taught <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/silva/dh/courses/mamsc/optionalmodules">optional modules</a> that are elective.</p>

<h2 class="heading"> Term Three</h2>





<p class="p"> This is for coursework assignments, exams and the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony/workplacements" target="_blank">Workplacement Module</a> and is followed by the
<a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony/dissertations" target="_blank">dissertation</a> (60 credits). 
</p>

<h2 class="heading">Further information</h2>





<ul class="disc">
<li>Some suggestions for <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/silva/dh/courses/mamsc/DHpreliminaryreading.pdf" target="_self">preliminary reading</a>.</li>
</ul>
<ul class="disc">
<li>For background on Digital Humanities see <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/events/archive/susanhockey" target="_self">The Susan Hockey Lecture in Digital Humanities </a>(video 63.52 mins)</li>
<li>For international students: <a href="http://www.prepareforsuccess.org.uk/" target="_self">Prepare for success</a> (Learning activities to prepare you for study in the UK)</li>
<li>Term Dates: <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/staff/term-dates/2017-2018" target="_blank">2017-2018</a></li>
<li>Useful information about <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/accommodation" target="_blank">Student Accommodation</a></li>
<li>Information for new students <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/occasional/information-new-students" target="_blank">2017-18</a></li>
</ul>
<p class="p">                  Academic enquiries should go to the Programme Director, <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/juliannenyhan" target="_blank">Julianne Nyhan</a> <br /></p>
<p class="p">                  Admissions enquiries should go to Sarah Davenport (<a href="mailto:s.davenport@ucl.ac.uk" target="_self">s.davenport@ucl.ac.uk</a>) <br /></p>
<p class="p">                  Core teaching staff
include:</p>
<ul class="disc">
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/simon-mahony/" target="_blank">Simon Mahony</a> </li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/julianne-nyhan/" target="_blank">Julianne Nyhan </a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/oliverdukewilliams" target="_blank">Oliver Duke-Williams</a> </li>
</ul>
<p class="p">                    A variety of other
teaching staff from across various departments at UCL will also teach
on the programme, depending on modules chosen.  
</p>

<h3 class="heading"></h3>





<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading">Entry requirements</h3>





<p class="p">                  Potential applicants
need to have a first or upper second-class Honours degree in
a relevant Humanities or Computing discipline from a UK university,
or an overseas qualification of an equivalent standard.<br /></p>
<p class="p"> <strong>Please note that we DO NOT accept applications from agencies and we will not communicate with an agent regarding your application. We expect all applicants to complete their applications themselves.</strong></p>
<p class="p">       The <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/life/international" target="_self">English Language Proficiency Requirement</a>
 for all non-native English speakers is<br /></p>
<ul class="disc">
<li>IELTS: a minimum of 7.0 with no less than 6.5 in each sub-set. </li>
<li>TOEFL: a minimum overall score of 100 with 24/30 in reading and writing and 20/30 in speaking and listening.</li>
</ul>
<p class="p"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/clie/graduate-preparation-courses/pre-sessional" target="_blank">Pre-sessional English courses</a>
 are available to introduce students to the UK academic 
culture as well as improving written and spoken English. Attendance on 
these courses does not guarantee that you will be accepted onto the 
programme. <br /></p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading">Fees: 2017-2018 session</h3>








<h5 class="heading">Full-time MA/MSc</h5>



<p class="p">                UK/EU students: £9,290<br />Overseas students: £20,005</p>



<h5 class="heading">         Part time: 2 years</h5>



<p class="p">pro-rata<br /></p>



<h5 class="heading">Flexible (modular): up to 5 years</h5>



<p class="p">       pro-rata depending on the number of credits taken per year.</p>



<h5 class="heading">Diploma and Certificate
</h5>



<p class="p">  details are on the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/current-students/money/2017-2018_fees" target="_self">UCL Fee Schedule: Postgraduate Taught 2017-2018</a></p>
<hr class="rule" />
<p class="p"><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/current-students/money/2016-2017_fees/2016-17_postgrad_taught" target="_blank"></a></p>

<h3 class="heading"></h3>






<h3 class="heading">Funding</h3>





<p class="p">                  For funding details
please visit <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/scholarships" target="_self">Scholarships and Funding</a>.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading"></h3>






<h3 class="heading">How to apply</h3>





<p class="p">                To apply online: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/taught/degrees/digital-humanities-ma-msc" target="_self">Application and entry</a>. <br /></p>
<p class="p"> <strong>Note that UCL admissions will not accept applications after 28th July.</strong></p>

                        <article class="article clearfix">
                            <!-- Start Silva content --> 

<a class="image" href="http://youtu.be/E2KzTPnU0Eo" title="UCLDH MA/MSc Video" target="_self"><img src="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/silva/dh/images/ucldh-mamsc-video-400.jpg" width="400" height="325" alt="UCLDH MA/MSc Video" class="medium-image" title="UCLDH MA/MSc Video" /></a><p class="p"><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc/e-brochure"></a>   Watch the <a href="http://youtu.be/E2KzTPnU0Eo" target="_self">UCLDH video</a> on YouTube (alternative <a href="http://v.youku.com/v_show/id_XNjI5NzAwOTU2.html" target="_blank">link</a>)!</p>

<h2 class="heading"></h2>





<hr class="rule" />

<h2 class="heading">Entry requirements</h2>





<p class="p">                  Potential applicants
need to have a first or upper second-class Honours degree in
a relevant Humanities or Computing discipline from a UK university,
or an overseas qualification of an equivalent standard.<br /></p>
<p class="p"> <strong>Please note that we DO NOT accept applications from agencies and we will not communicate with an agent regarding your application. We expect all applicants to complete their applications themselves.</strong></p>
<p class="p">       The <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/life/international" target="_self">English Language Proficiency Requirement</a>
 for all non-native English speakers is<br /></p>
<ul class="disc">
<li>IELTS: a minimum of 7.0 with no less than 6.5 in each sub-set. </li>
<li>TOEFL: a minimum overall score of 100 with 24/30 in reading and writing and 20/30 in speaking and listening.</li>
</ul>
<p class="p"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/clie/graduate-preparation-courses/pre-sessional" target="_blank">Pre-sessional English courses</a>
 are available to introduce students to the UK academic 
culture as well as improving written and spoken English. Attendance on 
these courses does not guarantee that you will be accepted onto the 
programme. <br /></p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h2 class="heading">Fees: 2017-2018 session</h2>








<h4 class="heading">Full-time MA/MSc</h4>



<p class="p">                UK/EU students: £9,290<br />Overseas students: £20,005</p>



<h4 class="heading">         Part time: 2 years</h4>



<p class="p">pro-rata<br /></p>



<h4 class="heading">Flexible (modular): up to 5 years</h4>



<p class="p">       pro-rata depending on the number of credits taken per year.</p>



<h4 class="heading">Diploma and Certificate
</h4>



<p class="p">  details are on the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/current-students/money/2017-2018_fees" target="_self">UCL Fee Schedule: Postgraduate Taught 2017-2018</a></p>
<hr class="rule" />
<p class="p"><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/current-students/money/2016-2017_fees/2016-17_postgrad_taught" target="_blank"></a></p>

<h2 class="heading"></h2>






<h2 class="heading">Funding</h2>





<p class="p">                  For funding details
please visit <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/scholarships" target="_self">Scholarships and Funding</a>.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h2 class="heading"></h2>






<h2 class="heading">How to apply</h2>





<p class="p">                To apply online: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/taught/degrees/digital-humanities-ma-msc" target="_self">Application and entry</a>. <br /></p>
<p class="p"> <strong>Note that UCL admissions will not accept applications after 28th July.</strong></p>
<hr class="rule" />
<a class="image" href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/taught/degrees/digital-humanities-ma-msc" title="Apply Now" target="_self"><div class="no-respond image-center"><img src="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/silva/dh/courses/mamsc/apply-now.png" width="90" height="90" alt="Apply Now" class="no-respond image-center" title="Apply Now" /></div></a>

<!-- End Silva content --> 

                        </article>

<h1 class="heading">Optional Modules</h1>
<p class="lead">    The UCLDH <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc" target="_self">MA/MSc Programme</a> includes the following optional modules. Please note that they are offered subject to availability, and certain modules may not run in each year. For any of these modules, students may be required to fulfil specific prerequisites. A full list of those available will be given to new students during Induction Week.</p>
<p class="p"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/lifesciences-faculty-php/courses/viewcourse.php?coursecode=PSYCGI15" target="_self">Affective Interaction</a><br /><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/current_students/syllabus/compgc/compgc26_artificial_intelligence_and_neural_computing/" target="_self">Artificial Intelligence and Neural Computing</a>*<br /><a href="http://www.bartlett.ucl.ac.uk/architecture/programmes/postgraduate/space-syntax-msc-mres-architectural-computation" target="_self">Computational Analysis</a><br /><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/current_students/syllabus/compgv/compgv15_computational_photography_and_capture/" target="_self">Computational Photography and Capture</a>*<br /><a href="http://www.bartlett.ucl.ac.uk/architecture/programmes/postgraduate/space-syntax-msc-mres-architectural-computation" target="_self">Computational Synthesis</a><br /><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/students/syllabus/msccs/gc20_computer_music/" target="_self">Computer Music</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/archaeology/studying/masters/courses/ARCLG209" target="_self">Cultural Heritage, Globalisation and Development</a><br /><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/anthropology/courses/pg" target="_self">Digital Infrastructure: Materiality, Information and Politics</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG038" target="_self">Electronic Publishing</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG083" target="_self">Foundations of Machine Learning</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG053" target="_self">Fundamentals of Information Science</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/archaeology/studying/masters/courses/ARCLG090" target="_self">Geographic Information Systems in Archaeology</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/archaeology/studying/masters/courses/ARCLG117" target="_self">Spatial Statistics, Network Analysis and Human History</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG012" target="_self">Historical Bibliography</a> <br /><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/current_students/syllabus/compgv/compgv12_image_processing/" target="_self">Image Processing</a> <br /> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG042-DH" target="_self">Individual Approved Study</a><br /><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/current_students/syllabus/compgc/compgc25_interaction_design/" target="_self">Interaction Design</a><br /> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG064" target="_self">Introduction to Digital Curation</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG063" target="_self">Introduction to Digitisation</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG062" target="_self">Knowledge Representation and Semantic Technologies</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG019" target="_self">Legal and Social Aspects of Electronic Publishing</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG022" target="_self">Manuscript Studies</a><br /><a href="https://sp.cege.ucl.ac.uk/study/Pages/Module-Guide.aspx?ModileCd=CEGEG034" target="_self">Mapping Science</a><br /><a href="http://development.rc.ucl.ac.uk/training/rcwithcpp" target="_self">Research Computing with C++ </a>*<br /> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/archaeology/studying/masters/courses/ARCLG118" target="_self">Research Skills for Spatial Analysis</a><br /><a href="http://development.rc.ucl.ac.uk/training/engineering" target="_self">Research Software Engineering with Python</a>*<br /><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/lifesciences-faculty-php/courses/viewcourse.php?coursecode=PSYCGI09" target="_self">Sociotechnical Systems: IT and the Future of Work </a><br /><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/current_students/syllabus/compgc/compgc22_software_engineering/" target="_self">Software Engineering</a>*<br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/archaeology/studying/masters/courses/ARCLG117" target="_self">Spatial Statistics, Network Analysis and Human History</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG035" target="_self">Systems Management</a><br /><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/eme/study/modules/unstitching" target="_self">Unstitching the Early Modern: Archival and Book Skills</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/eme/study/modules/web01" target="_self">Web 0.1: Early Modern Information Culture, c.1450-c.1750</a></p>
<p class="p">   *Note that these modules have significant prerequisites; for more details see the module page or the programme <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc/UCLDH_MaMSc_Supplementary2016.pdf" target="_self">supplementary prospectus.</a> </p>
<p class="p">    In addition to those listed above, subject to agreement of the module tutor and Programme Director, one module may be taken from any of those offered in the faculties of:</p>
<ul class="disc">
<li> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/ah" target="_blank">Arts and Humanities</a></li>
<li> <a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/" target="_blank">Computer Science</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/shs" target="_blank">Social and Historical Studies</a></li>
</ul>

<h3 class="heading"></h3>





<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading">Entry requirements</h3>





<p class="p">                  Potential applicants
need to have a first or upper second-class Honours degree in
a relevant Humanities or Computing discipline from a UK university,
or an overseas qualification of an equivalent standard.<br /></p>
<p class="p"> <strong>Please note that we DO NOT accept applications from agencies and we will not communicate with an agent regarding your application. We expect all applicants to complete their applications themselves.</strong></p>
<p class="p">       The <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/life/international" target="_self">English Language Proficiency Requirement</a>
 for all non-native English speakers is<br /></p>
<ul class="disc">
<li>IELTS: a minimum of 7.0 with no less than 6.5 in each sub-set. </li>
<li>TOEFL: a minimum overall score of 100 with 24/30 in reading and writing and 20/30 in speaking and listening.</li>
</ul>
<p class="p"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/clie/graduate-preparation-courses/pre-sessional" target="_blank">Pre-sessional English courses</a>
 are available to introduce students to the UK academic 
culture as well as improving written and spoken English. Attendance on 
these courses does not guarantee that you will be accepted onto the 
programme. <br /></p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading">Fees: 2017-2018 session</h3>








<h5 class="heading">Full-time MA/MSc</h5>



<p class="p">                UK/EU students: £9,290<br />Overseas students: £20,005</p>



<h5 class="heading">         Part time: 2 years</h5>



<p class="p">pro-rata<br /></p>



<h5 class="heading">Flexible (modular): up to 5 years</h5>



<p class="p">       pro-rata depending on the number of credits taken per year.</p>



<h5 class="heading">Diploma and Certificate
</h5>



<p class="p">  details are on the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/current-students/money/2017-2018_fees" target="_self">UCL Fee Schedule: Postgraduate Taught 2017-2018</a></p>
<hr class="rule" />
<p class="p"><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/current-students/money/2016-2017_fees/2016-17_postgrad_taught" target="_blank"></a></p>

<h3 class="heading"></h3>






<h3 class="heading">Funding</h3>





<p class="p">                  For funding details
please visit <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/scholarships" target="_self">Scholarships and Funding</a>.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading"></h3>






<h3 class="heading">How to apply</h3>





<p class="p">                To apply online: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/taught/degrees/digital-humanities-ma-msc" target="_self">Application and entry</a>. <br /></p>
<p class="p"> <strong>Note that UCL admissions will not accept applications after 28th July.</strong></p>
<hr class="rule" />
<a class="image" href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/taught/degrees/digital-humanities-ma-msc" title="Apply Now" target="_self"><div class="no-respond image-center"><img src="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/silva/dh/courses/mamsc/apply-now.png" width="90" height="90" alt="Apply Now" class="no-respond image-center" title="Apply Now" /></div></a>

                        <article class="article clearfix">

<h1 class="heading">Short Courses in DH</h1>

<h2 class="heading"></h2>





<img src="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/silva/dh/images/tower-boat.png" width="149" height="148" alt="tower boat" class="no-respond float-right" title="tower boat" /><p class="lead"> In addition to the full Master's programme, the following short courses in Digital Humanities are also offered by the department.</p>

<h2 class="heading"></h2>






<h2 class="heading">Certificate in Digital Humanities</h2>





<p class="p"> This is a very flexible programme for anyone looking to extend their skill set, particularly for CPD. Students registered for the Certificate must complete four modules from our DH core and options list as agreed with the Programme Director. The length of time taken depends on the student's circumstances (they may be working full-time or using this programme to complement other studies) and can range from a single term to a maximum of two years.    </p>
<p class="p"> The course unit value is 60 credits or 24 ECTS which are transferable in the UK and EU.<br /></p>
<p class="p"> Application is through the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/taught/degrees/digital-humanities-ma-msc" target="_self">UCL portal</a> and the fees are pro-rata (by credits) depending on those for the full Master's programme. </p>

<h2 class="heading">Diploma in Digital Humanities</h2>





<p class="p"> Again this is a very flexible programme with students taking all five core modules from the full Master's programme and a further three from the optional modules list. Diploma students do not take the workplacement or dissertation modules. This can be completed full-time over nine months or by flexible study over two to five years.</p>
<p class="p"> The course unit value is 120 credits or 48 ECTS which are transferable in the UK and EU. </p>
<p class="p"> Under the current UCL regulations for the Accreditation of Prior Learning (APL) credit transfer, a student who has already completed a PG Diploma and then applies for the Master’s programme will receive APL of 120 credits; this means that students holding a Diploma in DH would only need to complete the Dissertation to receive the full Master's degree. <br /></p>
<p class="p"> Application is through the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/taught/degrees/digital-humanities-ma-msc" target="_self">UCL portal</a> and the fees are pro-rata (by credits) depending on those for the full Master's programme. <br /></p>

<h2 class="heading">Graduate Affiliate Studies</h2>





<p class="p"> If you are currently enrolled at another institution it may be possible for you to study at our department to complement your work. Students usually come for one term and with this <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/international/affiliate/graduate/" target="_self">scheme</a>, although it is not possible to receive a UCL qualification, it is usually possible to count credit taken here towards the degree in the home institution. This would need to be confirmed with the home institution first.  </p>

<h2 class="heading">Individual Short Course modules</h2>





<p class="p">          Many of the modules that are offered by the Department of Information Studies as part of the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc" target="_blank">MA/MSc in Digital Humanities</a> programme work as stand-alone short courses for those wishing to update their professional skills in a particular area.</p>
<p class="p"> The modules are taught over one term, usually for one morning or one afternoon per week with 30 taught hours of lectures and practicals, followed by a coursework assessment or exam (which is optional for short course students). If the assessment is completed successfully, the module credit can count towards a future Master's degree.<br /></p>
<p class="p"> Many of these modules are CILIP accredited and so suitable for CPD for Library and Information professionals.<br /></p>
<p class="p">          DH modules currently offered as Short Courses include:</p>
<p class="p"> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG008" target="_blank">Digital Resources in the Humanities</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG038" target="_blank">Electronic Publishing</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG017" target="_blank">Internet Technologies</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank">Introduction to Programming and Scripting </a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG019" target="_blank">Legal and Social Aspects of Electronic Publishing</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank">Server Programming and Structured Data</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank">XML</a></p>
<p class="p"> Acceptance onto the module is by agreement by the tutor.  Many other modules from taught programmes offered by UCL Department of Information Studies (DIS) are available as <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/short-courses-cpd-information-studies" target="_self">short courses</a>. Details about fees and how to apply are also available on that page. <br /></p>



<h4 class="heading"></h4>





<!-- End Silva content -->

                     <div class="content-sidebar">
                                        <div class="site-content__sidebar">

<h3 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc">MA/MSc in DigitalHumanities</a> </h3>





<p class="p"> The <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/silva/dh/courses/short/mamsc">MA/MSc programme</a>, offered via <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis">UCL Department of Information Studies</a>,  is a new interdisciplinary degree exploring the intersection of digital technologies and culture.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/PhD">Doctorates</a> </h3>





<p class="p"> We have a variety of <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/doctorates" target="_self">doctoral students</a>
 who are undertaking research with us, and are interested in hearing 
from those who are considering undertaking PhD research in Digital 
Humanities. </p>

                        <article class="article clearfix">
                            <!-- Start Silva content --> 


<h2 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc">MA/MSc in DigitalHumanities</a> </h2>





<p class="p"> The <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/silva/dh/courses/short/mamsc">MA/MSc programme</a>, offered via <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis">UCL Department of Information Studies</a>,  is a new interdisciplinary degree exploring the intersection of digital technologies and culture.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h2 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/PhD">Doctorates</a> </h2>





<p class="p"> We have a variety of <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/doctorates" target="_self">doctoral students</a>
 who are undertaking research with us, and are interested in hearing 
from those who are considering undertaking PhD research in Digital 
Humanities. </p>


<!-- End Silva content --> 

                        </article>

                    <div class="content-footer">
                                        <hr />
                <div id="content-footer"></div>

                    </div>

                    </div>
                     <div class="content-sidebar">
                                        <div class="site-content__sidebar">

<h3 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc">MA/MSc in DigitalHumanities</a> </h3>





<p class="p"> The <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/silva/dh/courses/short/mamsc">MA/MSc programme</a>, offered via <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis">UCL Department of Information Studies</a>,  is a new interdisciplinary degree exploring the intersection of digital technologies and culture.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/PhD">Doctorates</a> </h3>





<p class="p"> We have a variety of <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/doctorates" target="_self">doctoral students</a>
 who are undertaking research with us, and are interested in hearing 
from those who are considering undertaking PhD research in Digital 
Humanities. </p>

                        <article class="article clearfix">
                            <!-- Start Silva content --> 
<h1 class="heading">MA/MSc in Digital Humanities</h1>
<p class="lead">The Master's degree in
Digital Humanities at UCL draws together teaching from a wide range
of disciplines, to investigate the application of computational
technologies to the arts, humanities, and cultural heritage. </p>
<p class="p"> The MA/MSc in Digital
Humanities is a truly interdisciplinary programme and has strong teaching links with: </p>
<ul class="disc">
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis" target="_self">UCL Department of Information Studies</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/" target="_self">UCL
Computer Science</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/ah/" target="_self">Arts and Humanities</a></li>
<li> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/shs/" target="_self">Social and Historical
Sciences</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/engineering/" target="_self">Engineering Science</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.bartlett.ucl.ac.uk/index.php" target="_self">Bartlett Faculty of the Built
Environment</a>. </li>
</ul>
<p class="p">       The programme also draws on facilities offered by:</p>
<ul class="disc">
<li> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/library/" target="_self">UCL Library Services</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/library/special-coll/" target="_self">Special Collections</a></li>
<li><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/museums/" target="_self">UCL Museums
and Collections</a></li>
</ul>
<p class="p">       as well as liaising closely with a variety of
world-class, London based libraries, archives, and museums within the
vicinity of UCL.</p>

<h2 class="heading">About the Programme</h2>





<p class="p">      The MA/MSc provides research-led teaching delivered by leading scholars.</p>
<p class="p">                  In
Term 1 and 2, students take five core modules, plus a further
three from a wide range of options available from various departments and
faculties at UCL. In addition, students write an original <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony/dissertations" target="_blank">dissertation</a> on a topic of their choice in consultation with their supervisor,
and undertake a <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony/workplacements" target="_blank">workplacement</a> at a related institution where they can apply
taught aspects of the programme in Term 3. This allows students who have a
background in the humanities to acquire necessarily skills in digital
technologies, and also makes it possible for those with a technical
background to become informed about scholarly methods in the humanities.</p>

<h2 class="heading">Terms One and Two</h2>





<p class="p"> The following core modules are mandatory for the programme:</p>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG008" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG008" target="_self">Digital Resources in the Humanities</a><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG008" target="_self"></a> </dt>
  <dd><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG008" target="_blank"></a>Introducing a range of
issues involved in the design, creation, management and use of
digital resources in the humanities. 
</dd>
</dl>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG017" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG017" target="_self">Internet
Technologies</a><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG017" target="_self"></a> </dt>
  <dd>Exploring the basic concepts of markup, website structuring and design, and issues involved in generating, evaluating and delivering online content. 
</dd>
</dl>
<p class="p"> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG017" target="_blank"></a></p>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank">Introduction to Programming and Scripting</a> </dt>
  <dd><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank"></a>      Providing an introduction to the key concepts and 
principles of standard procedural computer programming and a brief 
introduction to relational database querying and manipulation.</dd>
</dl>
<p class="p"> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank"></a></p>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank">Server Programming and Structured Data</a> </dt>
  <dd><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank"></a>Covering approaches to creating database driven 
websites, with a focus on applications relating to maps and spatial 
data. </dd>
</dl>
<p class="p"> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank"></a></p>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank">XML</a> </dt>
  <dd><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank"></a>Providing an overview
of Extensible Markup language; giving students the opportunity to
practice XML markup techniques, processing with XSLT, and demonstrating the use of XML in
publishing.</dd>
</dl>
<p class="p"> Note that the technical core modules are all at entry level; for 
students that already have demonstrable competencies in these areas, it 
may be possible, subject to the agreement of the Programme Director, to 
substitute modules from other UCL departments.</p>
<p class="p"> There are also a wide range of taught <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/silva/dh/courses/mamsc/optionalmodules">optional modules</a> that are elective.</p>

<h2 class="heading"> Term Three</h2>





<p class="p"> This is for coursework assignments, exams and the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony/workplacements" target="_blank">Workplacement Module</a> and is followed by the
<a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony/dissertations" target="_blank">dissertation</a> (60 credits). 
</p>

<h2 class="heading">Further information</h2>





<ul class="disc">
<li>Some suggestions for <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/silva/dh/courses/mamsc/DHpreliminaryreading.pdf" target="_self">preliminary reading</a>.</li>
</ul>
<ul class="disc">
<li>For background on Digital Humanities see <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/events/archive/susanhockey" target="_self">The Susan Hockey Lecture in Digital Humanities </a>(video 63.52 mins)</li>
<li>For international students: <a href="http://www.prepareforsuccess.org.uk/" target="_self">Prepare for success</a> (Learning activities to prepare you for study in the UK)</li>
<li>Term Dates: <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/staff/term-dates/2017-2018" target="_blank">2017-2018</a></li>
<li>Useful information about <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/accommodation" target="_blank">Student Accommodation</a></li>
<li>Information for new students <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/occasional/information-new-students" target="_blank">2017-18</a></li>
</ul>
<p class="p">                  Academic enquiries should go to the Programme Director, <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/juliannenyhan" target="_blank">Julianne Nyhan</a> <br /></p>
<p class="p">                  Admissions enquiries should go to Sarah Davenport (<a href="mailto:s.davenport@ucl.ac.uk" target="_self">s.davenport@ucl.ac.uk</a>) <br /></p>
<p class="p">                  Core teaching staff
include:</p>
<ul class="disc">
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/simon-mahony/" target="_blank">Simon Mahony</a> </li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/julianne-nyhan/" target="_blank">Julianne Nyhan </a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/oliverdukewilliams" target="_blank">Oliver Duke-Williams</a> </li>
</ul>
<p class="p">                    A variety of other
teaching staff from across various departments at UCL will also teach
on the programme, depending on modules chosen.  
</p>


<!-- End Silva content --> 

                        </article>

<a class="image" href="http://youtu.be/E2KzTPnU0Eo" title="UCLDH MA/MSc Video" target="_self"><img src="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/silva/dh/images/ucldh-mamsc-video-400.jpg" width="400" height="325" alt="UCLDH MA/MSc Video" class="medium-image" title="UCLDH MA/MSc Video" /></a><p class="p"><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc/e-brochure"></a>   Watch the <a href="http://youtu.be/E2KzTPnU0Eo" target="_self">UCLDH video</a> on YouTube (alternative <a href="http://v.youku.com/v_show/id_XNjI5NzAwOTU2.html" target="_blank">link</a>)!</p>

<h3 class="heading"></h3>





<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading">Entry requirements</h3>





<p class="p">                  Potential applicants
need to have a first or upper second-class Honours degree in
a relevant Humanities or Computing discipline from a UK university,
or an overseas qualification of an equivalent standard.<br /></p>
<p class="p"> <strong>Please note that we DO NOT accept applications from agencies and we will not communicate with an agent regarding your application. We expect all applicants to complete their applications themselves.</strong></p>
<p class="p">       The <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/life/international" target="_self">English Language Proficiency Requirement</a>
 for all non-native English speakers is<br /></p>
<ul class="disc">
<li>IELTS: a minimum of 7.0 with no less than 6.5 in each sub-set. </li>
<li>TOEFL: a minimum overall score of 100 with 24/30 in reading and writing and 20/30 in speaking and listening.</li>
</ul>
<p class="p"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/clie/graduate-preparation-courses/pre-sessional" target="_blank">Pre-sessional English courses</a>
 are available to introduce students to the UK academic 
culture as well as improving written and spoken English. Attendance on 
these courses does not guarantee that you will be accepted onto the 
programme. <br /></p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading">Fees: 2017-2018 session</h3>








<h5 class="heading">Full-time MA/MSc</h5>



<p class="p">                UK/EU students: £9,290<br />Overseas students: £20,005</p>



<h5 class="heading">         Part time: 2 years</h5>



<p class="p">pro-rata<br /></p>



<h5 class="heading">Flexible (modular): up to 5 years</h5>



<p class="p">       pro-rata depending on the number of credits taken per year.</p>



<h5 class="heading">Diploma and Certificate
</h5>



<p class="p">  details are on the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/current-students/money/2017-2018_fees" target="_self">UCL Fee Schedule: Postgraduate Taught 2017-2018</a></p>
<hr class="rule" />
<p class="p"><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/current-students/money/2016-2017_fees/2016-17_postgrad_taught" target="_blank"></a></p>

<h3 class="heading"></h3>






<h3 class="heading">Funding</h3>





<p class="p">                  For funding details
please visit <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/scholarships" target="_self">Scholarships and Funding</a>.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading"></h3>






<h3 class="heading">How to apply</h3>





<p class="p">                To apply online: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/taught/degrees/digital-humanities-ma-msc" target="_self">Application and entry</a>. <br /></p>
<p class="p"> <strong>Note that UCL admissions will not accept applications after 28th July.</strong></p>

                        <article class="article clearfix">
                            <!-- Start Silva content --> 
<h1 class="heading">Studying Digital Humanities at UCL</h1>
<p class="lead">  The UCL Centre for Digital Humanities facilitates various opportunities for study at post-graduate level.</p>
<p class="p">  Digital Humanities is a multidisciplinary field, undertaking research at the intersection of digital technologies and humanities. It aims to produce applications and models that make possible new kinds of research, both in the humanities disciplines and in computer science and its allied technologies. It also studies the impact of these techniques on cultural heritage, memory institutions, libraries, archives, and digital culture.</p>
<figure class="caption-img">



<a href="http://youtu.be/E2KzTPnU0Eo">
<img class="caption-img__img full-width"
     src="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/images/mamsc-vid" alt="" />
</a>

<figcaption class="caption-img__body">


<div class="tag__heading--captioned-overlay-border"></div>
<p>Watch the <a href="http://youtu.be/E2KzTPnU0Eo" silva_href="http://youtu.be/E2KzTPnU0Eo" target="_self">UCLDH video</a> on YouTube (alternative video <a href="http://v.youku.com/v_show/id_XNjI5NzAwOTU2.html" silva_href="http://v.youku.com/v_show/id_XNjI5NzAwOTU2.html" target="_blank">link</a> to YouKu)</p>
</figcaption>

</figure>
<p class="p">The Centre for Digital Humanities is able to capitalise on UCL's world-leading strength in information studies, computer science, and the arts and humanities. It brings together work being done in the many different departments and centres at UCL. Our location in central London, surrounded by the greatest concentration of libraries and professional bodies in Europe, also makes it an ideal base for collaboration with organisations outside UCL, such as museums, galleries, libraries and archives.</p>


<!-- End Silva content --> 

                        </article>

                    <div class="content-footer">
                                        <hr />
                <div id="content-footer"></div>

                    </div>

                    </div>
                     <div class="content-sidebar">
                                        <div class="site-content__sidebar">

<h3 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc">MA/MSc in DigitalHumanities</a> </h3>





<p class="p">The <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc">MA/MSc programme</a>, offered via <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis">UCL Department of Information Studies</a>,  is a new interdisciplinary degree exploring the intersection of digital technologies and culture.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading"><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/short">Short Courses in DH</a> </h3>





<p class="p">It is also possible to study individual modules from the MA/MSc programme as <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/short" target="_self">Short Courses</a> such as:</p>
<ul class="disc">
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank">XML</a></li>
<li> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG017" target="_blank">Internet Technologies</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG008" target="_blank">Digital Resources in the Humanities</a></li>
</ul>
<p class="p"> These courses can contribute to professional development, and count towards the MA/MSc, should it be pursued further.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/PhD">Doctorates</a> </h3>





<p class="p">We have a variety of <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/doctorates" target="_self">doctoral students</a>
 who are undertaking research with us, and are interested in hearing 
from those who are considering undertaking PhD research in Digital 
Humanities. </p>

</div>

                    </div>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <!--noindex-->

         

         
              

<footer class="footer wrapper"> 
    <div class="footer__inner clearfix">
        
            <article class="block block--col-1">
              <h2 class="as-h5"></h2>
              
<a class="image" href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis" title="UCL-DIS" target="_self"><img src="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/images/ucldis999.png" width="300" height="55" alt="UCL-DIS" class="no-respond" title="UCL-DIS" /></a>

            </article>
        


        
            <article class="block block--col-2">
              <h2 class="as-h5"></h2>
              
<a class="image" href="http://eadh.org" title="European Association for Digital Humanities" target="_self"><img src="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/images/eadh.png" width="300" height="57" alt="European Association for Digital Humanities" class="no-respond" title="European Association for Digital Humanities" /></a>

            </article>

                        <article class="article clearfix">
                            <!-- Start Silva content --> 
<h1 class="heading">Doctorates at UCLDH</h1>
<a class="image" href="http://twitpic.com/3u3u7d" title="Doc" target="_self"><img src="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/images/231966121.jpg" width="150" height="150" alt="Doc" class="no-respond float-right" title="Doc" /></a><p class="lead">    UCL Centre for Digital Humanities facilitates the work of students currently carrying out PhD or EngD research, both from the UK and abroad.</p>
<p class="p">    PhDs at UCL are normally designed to extend over three years full-time or five years part-time study (unlike, say, North American PhDs there are no taught components prior to writing a thesis).  Further information about pursuing a PhD at UCL, and what it generally entails, can be found in the <a href="http://www.grad.ucl.ac.uk" target="_self">UCL Graduate School Research Programmes pages</a>. Most PhDs at UCLDH will, depending on their supervisor, be formally part of the Department of Information Studies (DIS), and UCL DIS provides <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/phd" target="_self"> further information about Research Degrees</a>. Those interested in more technical areas should also look at the <a href="http://engdveiv.cs.ucl.ac.uk/">UCL Engineering Doctorate (Virtual Environments Imaging and Visualisation)</a> pages, where funded EngD places will be advertised.</p>
<p class="p">    We recommend that before you make a formal application you discuss your potential research project with a member of staff at UCL. When you do so, please send a brief description of the topic that you would like to work on- of about a thousand words- and a copy of your CV. Please also copy this to the PhD student tutor of UCL Information Studies as they are responsible for all PhD student admissions in the department.</p>
<p class="p">    We are now receiving more enquiries from PhD students than we have places available. Therefore please be aware that admission is a competitive process, and be willing to take some time preparing your application, as a result. We make decisions about who to admit based on how well your proposed topic fits with UCLDH research and your academic track record. If accepted you will be matched with the members of staff whose interests most closely relate to your research topic: we cannot guarantee that you will be able to work with specific named individuals.</p>
<p class="p">    Funding for PhDs is limited and competitive, and potential students are expected to pursue all avenues themselves in attracting funding. The Graduate School provides further information about <a href="http://www.grad.ucl.ac.uk/funds/" target="_self">fees, costs and funding</a>, and the Arts and Humanities Research Council (AHRC) website lists their current <a href="http://www.ahrc.ac.uk/Funding-Opportunities/Postgraduate-funding/Pages/Postgraduate%20funding.aspx" target="_self">postgraduate funding opportunities</a>.</p>
<p class="p">    UCL is a partner in the London Arts and Humanities Partnership, an AHRC funded Doctoral Training Partnership offering studentships. Please see the <a href="http://www.lahp.ac.uk/apply-for-a-studentship/" target="_self">LAHP website</a> for further information and details on how to apply.</p>
<p class="p">    UCL is also a partner in the Engineering and Physical Sciences Research Council (EPSRC) funded <a href="http://www.seaha-cdt.ac.uk" target="_self">Centre for Doctoral Training in Science and Engineering in Arts, Heritage and Archaeology (SEAHA)</a>, which offers studentships to those interested in pursuing a PhD in heritage science.</p>

<h2 class="heading">Doctoral Students linked to UCLDH</h2>





<ul class="disc">
<li><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/people_new/C.Aspromallis.html/" target="_self"><strong>Christodoulos Aspromallis</strong></a> works on engineering reliable, robust, real-time generative music algorithms and systems for mixed-reality scenarios. His work involves computational gesture recognition and activity modelling linked to real-time algorithmic composition, and builds on probabilistic and other theoretical models of automated music generation. Supervisors: <a href="http://www0.cs.ucl.ac.uk/people/N.Gold.html" target="_self">Nicolas Gold</a> [first], <a href="http://www0.cs.ucl.ac.uk/people/S.Julier.html" target="_self">Simon Julier</a> [second].</li>
<li><strong><a href="http://www0.cs.ucl.ac.uk/staff/S.Garcia/" target="_self">Antonio García Castañeda</a></strong> works on the 'automatic reconstruction of fragmented frescoes and other cultural artefacts'. Supervisors: <a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/staff/t.weyrich/" target="_self">Tim Weyrich</a> [first].</li>
<li><strong><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/gretafranzini" target="_self">Greta Franzini</a></strong> is creating a digital edition of the oldest surviving manuscript of <em>S. </em>Augustine's <em>De Civitate Dei </em>and in so doing examining best practice in the field of electronic editing. Supervisors: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/melissa-terras/" target="_self">Melissa Terras</a> [first] and <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony" target="_self">Simon Mahony</a> [second].</li>
<li><strong><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/gao" target="_blank">Jin Gao</a> </strong>is working on citation network analysis and social network analysis of the Digital Humanities. Supervisors: <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/oliverdukewilliams" target="_blank">Oliver Duke-Williams</a> [first] and <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony" target="_blank">Simon Mahony</a>, <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/juliannenyhan" target="_blank">Julianne Nyhan</a>, <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/melanie" target="_blank">Melanie Ramdarshan Bold</a> [subsidiary team].</li>
<li><strong><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/kamposiori/" target="_self">Christina Kamposiori</a> </strong>works on<strong> </strong>'personal research collections: examining research practices and user needs in art historical research'. Supervisors: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony" target="_self">Simon Mahony</a> [first] and <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/juliannenyhan" target="_self">Julianne Nyhan</a>  [second].</li>
<li><strong>Helen O' Neill </strong> works on analysing reader records of the London Library. Supervisors: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/melissa-terras/" target="_self">Melissa Terras</a> [first] and<a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/annewelsh" target="_self"> Anne Welsh </a> [second].</li>
<li><strong>Ananda Rutherford </strong>works on critical
approaches to museum object records and the effect of digitisation on
collections information. Supervisors: Melissa Terras [first] and Haidy Geismar
[second].</li>
<li><strong>Kinda Dahlan </strong> works on Information Practices Across The Academic And Non-academic Fields of Oceanography. Supervisors: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/melissa-terras/" target="_self">Melissa Terras</a> [first] and<a href="http://www.geog.ucl.ac.uk/about-the-department/people/academic-staff/jon-french" target="_self"> Jon French</a> [second].</li>
<li><strong><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/routsis/" target="_self">Vasileios Routsis</a></strong> works on 'information technology and social control mechanisms: The evolution of the concept of privacy'<strong>. </strong>Supervisors: <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/antonis" target="_self">Antonis Bikakis</a><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/claire-warwick/" target="_self"></a> [first] and <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony" target="_self">Simon Mahony</a> [second].</li>
</ul>

<h2 class="heading">Affiliated Doctoral Students</h2>





<p class="p">    Affiliated PhD Students are those whose first supervisor is not from within UCLDH, but whose secondary supervisor is linked to the Centre.</p>
<ul class="disc">
<li><strong><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/postgrads?id=44656" target="_self">Paolo Casani</a></strong> works on examining the changes that ubiquitous internet and communication technologies (ICTs) induce into the aesthetic dimension by enacting new modes of perception, and how these in turn colour, filter and exclude aspects of how we come to understand our selves and the world. Supervisors: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/juliannenyhan" target="_self">Julianne Nyhan</a> [first] from the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis" target="_self">Department of Information Studies</a> and <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/andrewflinn" target="_self">Andrew Flinn</a> [second]</li>
<li><strong>Cerys Jones</strong> is using multispectral imaging to develop techniques for image acquisition and analysis for use in digital humanities, with the ultimate aim of developing standards for libraries, archives, galleries and museums to capture and process multispectral images. Supervisors: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/medphys/staff/people/agibson/www" target="_self">Adam Gibson</a>, [first] from the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/medphys/" target="_self">Department of Medical and Biomedical Engineering</a> and <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/melissaterras" target="_self">Melissa Terras</a> [second]</li>
<li><strong>Ian Maybury</strong> is researching the use of hyperspectral imaging (HSI) in a heritage context, learning how to best use the equipment to extract information such as hidden text, relief details, the presence of organic growth, and signs of deterioration. Supervisors: <a href="http://www.geog.ox.ac.uk/staff/hviles.html" target="_self">Heather Viles</a> [first], School of Geography and Environment, University of Oxford, and <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/melissaterras" target="_self">Melissa Terras</a> [second]</li>
<li><strong>Foteini Valeonti </strong>is utilising crowdsourcing and augmented reality in an attempt to make art more accessible, not only on the digital domain, but also in the physical space. Supervisors: <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/bartlett/casa/prof-andy-hudson-smith" target="_self">Andrew Hudson-Smith</a> [first] from the Bartlett Centre for Advanced Spatial Analysis and <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/melissaterras" target="_self">Melissa Terras</a> [second]</li>
</ul>

<h2 class="heading">Completed PhDs</h2>





<ul class="disc">
<li><strong>Isabel Galina</strong> worked on Open Access and Institutional Repositories. She is now coordinator for of the ReDHD Digital Humanities network in Latin America and works at the Institute for Bibliographic Studies at the Universidad Nacional Autónoma de México (UNAM). She was awarded her PhD in July 2009.
</li>
<li><strong>Ernesto Priego</strong> worked on Comic books in the Digital Age, and was awarded his PhD in May 2011</li>
<li><a href="http://esad.classics.ox.ac.uk/index.php?option=com_content&amp;view=article&amp;id=45&amp;Itemid=60" target="_self"><strong>Henriette Roued-Cunliffe</strong></a><strong> </strong>worked on 'a system to improve the interpretation of ancient documents', as part of the eSAD project for the <a href="http://www.classics.ox.ac.uk/index.asp" target="_self">Faculty of Classics at the University of Oxford</a>. Supervisors: <a href="http://www.classics.ox.ac.uk/faculty/directory/buscard.asp?IDno=78" target="_self">Alan Bowman</a> [first] and <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/melissa-terras/" target="_self">Melissa Terras</a> [second]. She was awarded her PhD in May 2012.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.tawawa.org/"><strong>Rudolf Ammann</strong></a> examined 'the formative stages and emergence of blogging'. Supervisors: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/melissa-terras/" target="_self">Melissa Terras</a> [first] and <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/clairewarwick/" target="_self">Claire Warwick</a> [second]. He was awarded his PhD in June 2013.</li>
<li><strong><a href="http://oddfish.co.uk/" target="_self">Susan Greenberg</a> </strong>worked on 'the poetics of editing in print and digital form'. Supervisors: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/iain-stevenson/" target="_self">Iain Stevenson</a> [first] and <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/claire-warwick/" target="_self">Claire Warwick</a> [second]. She was awarded her PhD in December 2013.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/medphys/phd/phdstudents/agiacometti" target="_self"><strong>Alejandro Giacometti</strong></a> was researching 'medical imaging methods and technologies and how they can be adapted in order to recover information from ancient documents'. Supervisors:  <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/medphys/staff/people/agibson" target="_self">Adam Gibson</a> [first] and  <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/melissa-terras/" target="_self">Melissa Terras</a> [second]. Affiliation: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/medphys/" target="_self">Department of Medical Physics and Bioengineering</a>. He was awarded his PhD in December 2013.</li>
<li><strong>Paul Gooding</strong> worked on 'Digitisation' with the <a href="http://www.bl.uk/" target="_self">British Library</a>. Supervisors: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/claire-warwick/" target="_self">Claire Warwick</a> [first] and <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/melissa-terras/" target="_self">Melissa Terras</a>. He was awarded his PhD in June 2014.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/claire-ross/" target="_self"><strong>Claire Ross</strong></a> worked on 'users' experience and information seeking behaviour of digital museum content'. Supervisors: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/melissa-terras/" target="_self">Melissa Terras</a> [first – covered by <a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/people/A.Blandford.html" target="_self">Ann Blandford</a> during leave] and <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/claire-warwick/" target="_self">Claire Warwick</a> [second]. She was awarded her PhD in June 2014.</li>
<li><strong>Lorna Richardson</strong> worked on 'public archaeology in the Digital Age'. Supervisors:<a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/melissa-terras/" target="_self">Melissa Terras</a> [first] and <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/archaeology/people/staff/schadla_hall" target="_self">Tim Schadla-Hall</a> [second]. She was awarded her PhD in July 2014.</li>
<li><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/staff/K.Pal/" target="_self"><strong>Kazim Pal</strong></a> worked on 'scanning work of the Grand Parchment' with the <a href="http://www.cityoflondon.gov.uk/Corporation/LGNL_Services/Leisure_and_culture/Records_and_archives/" target="_self">London Metropolitan Archives</a>. Supervisors: <a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/staff/t.weyrich/" target="_self">Tim Weyrich</a> [first] and <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/melissa-terras/" target="_self">Melissa Terras</a> [second]. He was awarded in July 2015.</li>
<li><strong>John Hindmarch</strong> worked on '3D scanning of science museum collections'. Supervisors: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/melissa-terras/" target="_self">Melissa Terras</a> [first] and<a href="http://www2.cege.ucl.ac.uk/staf/staffpage.asp?StaffID=683" target="_self"> Stuart Robson</a> [second].</li>
</ul>

                     <div class="content-sidebar">
                                        <div class="site-content__sidebar">

<h3 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc">MA/MSc in DigitalHumanities</a> </h3>





<p class="p"> The <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/doctorates/mamsc">MA/MSc programme</a>, offered via <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis">UCL Department of Information Studies</a>,  is a new interdisciplinary degree exploring the intersection of digital technologies and culture.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading"><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/short">Short Courses in DH</a> </h3>





<p class="p"> It is also possible to study individual modules from the MA/MSc programme as <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/short" target="_self">Short Courses</a> such as:</p>
<ul class="disc">
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank">XML</a></li>
<li> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG017" target="_blank">Internet Technologies</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG008" target="_blank">Digital Resources in the Humanities</a></li>
</ul>
<p class="p">  These courses can contribute to professional development, and count towards the MA/MSc, should it be pursued further.</p>

</div>

                    </div>
                </div>

                        <article class="article clearfix">
                            <!-- Start Silva content --> 


<h2 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc">MA/MSc in DigitalHumanities</a> </h2>





<p class="p">The <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc">MA/MSc programme</a>, offered via <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis">UCL Department of Information Studies</a>,  is a new interdisciplinary degree exploring the intersection of digital technologies and culture.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h2 class="heading"><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/short">Short Courses in DH</a> </h2>





<p class="p">It is also possible to study individual modules from the MA/MSc programme as <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/short" target="_self">Short Courses</a> such as:</p>
<ul class="disc">
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank">XML</a></li>
<li> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG017" target="_blank">Internet Technologies</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG008" target="_blank">Digital Resources in the Humanities</a></li>
</ul>
<p class="p"> These courses can contribute to professional development, and count towards the MA/MSc, should it be pursued further.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h2 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/PhD">Doctorates</a> </h2>





<p class="p">We have a variety of <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/doctorates" target="_self">doctoral students</a>
 who are undertaking research with us, and are interested in hearing 
from those who are considering undertaking PhD research in Digital 
Humanities. </p>


<!-- End Silva content --> 

                        </article>

                    <div class="content-footer">
                                        <hr />
                <div id="content-footer"></div>

                    </div>

                     <div class="content-sidebar">
                                        <div class="site-content__sidebar">

<h3 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc">MA/MSc in DigitalHumanities</a> </h3>





<p class="p">The <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc">MA/MSc programme</a>, offered via <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis">UCL Department of Information Studies</a>,  is a new interdisciplinary degree exploring the intersection of digital technologies and culture.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading"><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/short">Short Courses in DH</a> </h3>





<p class="p">It is also possible to study individual modules from the MA/MSc programme as <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/short" target="_self">Short Courses</a> such as:</p>
<ul class="disc">
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank">XML</a></li>
<li> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG017" target="_blank">Internet Technologies</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG008" target="_blank">Digital Resources in the Humanities</a></li>
</ul>
<p class="p"> These courses can contribute to professional development, and count towards the MA/MSc, should it be pursued further.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/PhD">Doctorates</a> </h3>





<p class="p">We have a variety of <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/doctorates" target="_self">doctoral students</a>
 who are undertaking research with us, and are interested in hearing 
from those who are considering undertaking PhD research in Digital 
Humanities. </p>

<h1 class="heading">MA/MSc in Digital Humanities</h1>
<p class="lead">The Master's degree in
Digital Humanities at UCL draws together teaching from a wide range
of disciplines, to investigate the application of computational
technologies to the arts, humanities, and cultural heritage. </p>
<p class="p"> The MA/MSc in Digital
Humanities is a truly interdisciplinary programme and has strong teaching links with: </p>
<ul class="disc">
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis" target="_self">UCL Department of Information Studies</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/" target="_self">UCL
Computer Science</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/ah/" target="_self">Arts and Humanities</a></li>
<li> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/shs/" target="_self">Social and Historical
Sciences</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/engineering/" target="_self">Engineering Science</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.bartlett.ucl.ac.uk/index.php" target="_self">Bartlett Faculty of the Built
Environment</a>. </li>
</ul>
<p class="p">       The programme also draws on facilities offered by:</p>
<ul class="disc">
<li> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/library/" target="_self">UCL Library Services</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/library/special-coll/" target="_self">Special Collections</a></li>
<li><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/museums/" target="_self">UCL Museums
and Collections</a></li>
</ul>
<p class="p">       as well as liaising closely with a variety of
world-class, London based libraries, archives, and museums within the
vicinity of UCL.</p>

<h2 class="heading">About the Programme</h2>





<p class="p">      The MA/MSc provides research-led teaching delivered by leading scholars.</p>
<p class="p">                  In
Term 1 and 2, students take five core modules, plus a further
three from a wide range of options available from various departments and
faculties at UCL. In addition, students write an original <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony/dissertations" target="_blank">dissertation</a> on a topic of their choice in consultation with their supervisor,
and undertake a <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony/workplacements" target="_blank">workplacement</a> at a related institution where they can apply
taught aspects of the programme in Term 3. This allows students who have a
background in the humanities to acquire necessarily skills in digital
technologies, and also makes it possible for those with a technical
background to become informed about scholarly methods in the humanities.</p>

<h2 class="heading">Terms One and Two</h2>





<p class="p"> The following core modules are mandatory for the programme:</p>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG008" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG008" target="_self">Digital Resources in the Humanities</a><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG008" target="_self"></a> </dt>
  <dd><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG008" target="_blank"></a>Introducing a range of
issues involved in the design, creation, management and use of
digital resources in the humanities. 
</dd>
</dl>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG017" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG017" target="_self">Internet
Technologies</a><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG017" target="_self"></a> </dt>
  <dd>Exploring the basic concepts of markup, website structuring and design, and issues involved in generating, evaluating and delivering online content. 
</dd>
</dl>
<p class="p"> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG017" target="_blank"></a></p>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank">Introduction to Programming and Scripting</a> </dt>
  <dd><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank"></a>      Providing an introduction to the key concepts and 
principles of standard procedural computer programming and a brief 
introduction to relational database querying and manipulation.</dd>
</dl>
<p class="p"> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank"></a></p>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank">Server Programming and Structured Data</a> </dt>
  <dd><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank"></a>Covering approaches to creating database driven 
websites, with a focus on applications relating to maps and spatial 
data. </dd>
</dl>
<p class="p"> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank"></a></p>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank">XML</a> </dt>
  <dd><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank"></a>Providing an overview
of Extensible Markup language; giving students the opportunity to
practice XML markup techniques, processing with XSLT, and demonstrating the use of XML in
publishing.</dd>
</dl>
<p class="p"> Note that the technical core modules are all at entry level; for 
students that already have demonstrable competencies in these areas, it 
may be possible, subject to the agreement of the Programme Director, to 
substitute modules from other UCL departments.</p>
<p class="p"> There are also a wide range of taught <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc/optionalmodules">optional modules</a> that are elective.</p>

<h2 class="heading"> Term Three</h2>





<p class="p"> This is for coursework assignments, exams and the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony/workplacements" target="_blank">Workplacement Module</a> and is followed by the
<a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony/dissertations" target="_blank">dissertation</a> (60 credits). 
</p>

<h2 class="heading">Further information</h2>





<ul class="disc">
<li>Some suggestions for <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc/DHpreliminaryreading.pdf" target="_self">preliminary reading</a>.</li>
</ul>
<ul class="disc">
<li>For background on Digital Humanities see <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/events/archive/susanhockey" target="_self">The Susan Hockey Lecture in Digital Humanities </a>(video 63.52 mins)</li>
<li>For international students: <a href="http://www.prepareforsuccess.org.uk/" target="_self">Prepare for success</a> (Learning activities to prepare you for study in the UK)</li>
<li>Term Dates: <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/staff/term-dates/2017-2018" target="_blank">2017-2018</a></li>
<li>Useful information about <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/accommodation" target="_blank">Student Accommodation</a></li>
<li>Information for new students <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/occasional/information-new-students" target="_blank">2017-18</a></li>
</ul>
<p class="p">                  Academic enquiries should go to the Programme Director, <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/juliannenyhan" target="_blank">Julianne Nyhan</a> <br /></p>
<p class="p">                  Admissions enquiries should go to Sarah Davenport (<a href="mailto:s.davenport@ucl.ac.uk" target="_self">s.davenport@ucl.ac.uk</a>) <br /></p>
<p class="p">                  Core teaching staff
include:</p>
<ul class="disc">
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/simon-mahony/" target="_blank">Simon Mahony</a> </li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/julianne-nyhan/" target="_blank">Julianne Nyhan </a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/oliverdukewilliams" target="_blank">Oliver Duke-Williams</a> </li>
</ul>
<p class="p">                    A variety of other
teaching staff from across various departments at UCL will also teach
on the programme, depending on modules chosen.  
</p>
