<h3 class="heading"></h3>





<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading">Entry requirements</h3>





<p class="p">                  Potential applicants
need to have a first or upper second-class Honours degree in
a relevant Humanities or Computing discipline from a UK university,
or an overseas qualification of an equivalent standard.<br /></p>
<p class="p"> <strong>Please note that we DO NOT accept applications from agencies and we will not communicate with an agent regarding your application. We expect all applicants to complete their applications themselves.</strong></p>
<p class="p">       The <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/life/international" target="_self">English Language Proficiency Requirement</a>
 for all non-native English speakers is<br /></p>
<ul class="disc">
<li>IELTS: a minimum of 7.0 with no less than 6.5 in each sub-set. </li>
<li>TOEFL: a minimum overall score of 100 with 24/30 in reading and writing and 20/30 in speaking and listening.</li>
</ul>
<p class="p"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/clie/graduate-preparation-courses/pre-sessional" target="_blank">Pre-sessional English courses</a>
 are available to introduce students to the UK academic 
culture as well as improving written and spoken English. Attendance on 
these courses does not guarantee that you will be accepted onto the 
programme. <br /></p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading">Fees: 2017-2018 session</h3>








<h5 class="heading">Full-time MA/MSc</h5>



<p class="p">                UK/EU students: £9,290<br />Overseas students: £20,005</p>



<h5 class="heading">         Part time: 2 years</h5>



<p class="p">pro-rata<br /></p>



<h5 class="heading">Flexible (modular): up to 5 years</h5>



<p class="p">       pro-rata depending on the number of credits taken per year.</p>



<h5 class="heading">Diploma and Certificate
</h5>



<p class="p">  details are on the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/current-students/money/2017-2018_fees" target="_self">UCL Fee Schedule: Postgraduate Taught 2017-2018</a></p>
<hr class="rule" />
<p class="p"><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/current-students/money/2016-2017_fees/2016-17_postgrad_taught" target="_blank"></a></p>

<h3 class="heading"></h3>






<h3 class="heading">Funding</h3>





<p class="p">                  For funding details
please visit <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/scholarships" target="_self">Scholarships and Funding</a>.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading"></h3>






<h3 class="heading">How to apply</h3>





<p class="p">                To apply online: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/taught/degrees/digital-humanities-ma-msc" target="_self">Application and entry</a>. <br /></p>
<p class="p"> <strong>Note that UCL admissions will not accept applications after 28th July.</strong></p>
<hr class="rule" />

  (iframe.frameElement || iframe).style.cssText = "width:0;height:0;border:0;display:none;";
  where = document.getElementsByTagName("script")[0];
  where.parentNode.insertBefore(iframe, where);

  try {
    doc = iframe.contentWindow.document;
  } catch(e) {
    dom = document.domain;
    iframe.src="javascript:var d=document.open();d.domain='"+dom+"';void(0);";
    doc = iframe.contentWindow.document;
  }
  doc.open()._l = function() {
    var js = this.createElement("script");
    if (dom) { this.domain = dom; }
    js.id = "boomr-if-as";
    js.src = "//c.go-mpulse.net/boomerang/" +
    "SUWW2-HAKPB-Q4WN7-TQ6VL-GTMT2";
    BOOMR_lstart=new Date().getTime();
    this.body.appendChild(js);
  };
  doc.write('<body onload="document._l();">');
  doc.close();
})();
</script>

                        <article class="article clearfix">
                            <!-- Start Silva content --> 

<a class="image" href="http://youtu.be/E2KzTPnU0Eo" title="UCLDH MA/MSc Video" target="_self"><img src="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/images/ucldh-mamsc-video-400.jpg" width="400" height="325" alt="UCLDH MA/MSc Video" class="medium-image" title="UCLDH MA/MSc Video" /></a><p class="p"><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc/e-brochure"></a>   Watch the <a href="http://youtu.be/E2KzTPnU0Eo" target="_self">UCLDH video</a> on YouTube (alternative <a href="http://v.youku.com/v_show/id_XNjI5NzAwOTU2.html" target="_blank">link</a>)!</p>

<h2 class="heading"></h2>





<hr class="rule" />

<h2 class="heading">Entry requirements</h2>





<p class="p">                  Potential applicants
need to have a first or upper second-class Honours degree in
a relevant Humanities or Computing discipline from a UK university,
or an overseas qualification of an equivalent standard.<br /></p>
<p class="p"> <strong>Please note that we DO NOT accept applications from agencies and we will not communicate with an agent regarding your application. We expect all applicants to complete their applications themselves.</strong></p>
<p class="p">       The <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/life/international" target="_self">English Language Proficiency Requirement</a>
 for all non-native English speakers is<br /></p>
<ul class="disc">
<li>IELTS: a minimum of 7.0 with no less than 6.5 in each sub-set. </li>
<li>TOEFL: a minimum overall score of 100 with 24/30 in reading and writing and 20/30 in speaking and listening.</li>
</ul>
<p class="p"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/clie/graduate-preparation-courses/pre-sessional" target="_blank">Pre-sessional English courses</a>
 are available to introduce students to the UK academic 
culture as well as improving written and spoken English. Attendance on 
these courses does not guarantee that you will be accepted onto the 
programme. <br /></p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h2 class="heading">Fees: 2017-2018 session</h2>








<h4 class="heading">Full-time MA/MSc</h4>



<p class="p">                UK/EU students: £9,290<br />Overseas students: £20,005</p>



<h4 class="heading">         Part time: 2 years</h4>



<p class="p">pro-rata<br /></p>



<h4 class="heading">Flexible (modular): up to 5 years</h4>



<p class="p">       pro-rata depending on the number of credits taken per year.</p>



<h4 class="heading">Diploma and Certificate
</h4>



<p class="p">  details are on the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/current-students/money/2017-2018_fees" target="_self">UCL Fee Schedule: Postgraduate Taught 2017-2018</a></p>
<hr class="rule" />
<p class="p"><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/current-students/money/2016-2017_fees/2016-17_postgrad_taught" target="_blank"></a></p>

<h2 class="heading"></h2>






<h2 class="heading">Funding</h2>





<p class="p">                  For funding details
please visit <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/scholarships" target="_self">Scholarships and Funding</a>.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h2 class="heading"></h2>






<h2 class="heading">How to apply</h2>





<p class="p">                To apply online: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/taught/degrees/digital-humanities-ma-msc" target="_self">Application and entry</a>. <br /></p>
<p class="p"> <strong>Note that UCL admissions will not accept applications after 28th July.</strong></p>
<hr class="rule" />
<a class="image" href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/taught/degrees/digital-humanities-ma-msc" title="Apply Now" target="_self"><div class="no-respond image-center"><img src="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc/apply-now.png" width="90" height="90" alt="Apply Now" class="no-respond image-center" title="Apply Now" /></div></a>

<!-- End Silva content --> 

                        </article>

                    <div class="content-footer">
                                        <hr />

                    </div>

                    </div>

<h1 class="heading">Optional Modules</h1>
<p class="lead">    The UCLDH <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc" target="_self">MA/MSc Programme</a> includes the following optional modules. Please note that they are offered subject to availability, and certain modules may not run in each year. For any of these modules, students may be required to fulfil specific prerequisites. A full list of those available will be given to new students during Induction Week.</p>
<p class="p"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/lifesciences-faculty-php/courses/viewcourse.php?coursecode=PSYCGI15" target="_self">Affective Interaction</a><br /><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/current_students/syllabus/compgc/compgc26_artificial_intelligence_and_neural_computing/" target="_self">Artificial Intelligence and Neural Computing</a>*<br /><a href="http://www.bartlett.ucl.ac.uk/architecture/programmes/postgraduate/space-syntax-msc-mres-architectural-computation" target="_self">Computational Analysis</a><br /><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/current_students/syllabus/compgv/compgv15_computational_photography_and_capture/" target="_self">Computational Photography and Capture</a>*<br /><a href="http://www.bartlett.ucl.ac.uk/architecture/programmes/postgraduate/space-syntax-msc-mres-architectural-computation" target="_self">Computational Synthesis</a><br /><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/students/syllabus/msccs/gc20_computer_music/" target="_self">Computer Music</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/archaeology/studying/masters/courses/ARCLG209" target="_self">Cultural Heritage, Globalisation and Development</a><br /><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/anthropology/courses/pg" target="_self">Digital Infrastructure: Materiality, Information and Politics</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG038" target="_self">Electronic Publishing</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG083" target="_self">Foundations of Machine Learning</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG053" target="_self">Fundamentals of Information Science</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/archaeology/studying/masters/courses/ARCLG090" target="_self">Geographic Information Systems in Archaeology</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/archaeology/studying/masters/courses/ARCLG117" target="_self">Spatial Statistics, Network Analysis and Human History</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG012" target="_self">Historical Bibliography</a> <br /><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/current_students/syllabus/compgv/compgv12_image_processing/" target="_self">Image Processing</a> <br /> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG042-DH" target="_self">Individual Approved Study</a><br /><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/current_students/syllabus/compgc/compgc25_interaction_design/" target="_self">Interaction Design</a><br /> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG064" target="_self">Introduction to Digital Curation</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG063" target="_self">Introduction to Digitisation</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG062" target="_self">Knowledge Representation and Semantic Technologies</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG019" target="_self">Legal and Social Aspects of Electronic Publishing</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG022" target="_self">Manuscript Studies</a><br /><a href="https://sp.cege.ucl.ac.uk/study/Pages/Module-Guide.aspx?ModileCd=CEGEG034" target="_self">Mapping Science</a><br /><a href="http://development.rc.ucl.ac.uk/training/rcwithcpp" target="_self">Research Computing with C++ </a>*<br /> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/archaeology/studying/masters/courses/ARCLG118" target="_self">Research Skills for Spatial Analysis</a><br /><a href="http://development.rc.ucl.ac.uk/training/engineering" target="_self">Research Software Engineering with Python</a>*<br /><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/lifesciences-faculty-php/courses/viewcourse.php?coursecode=PSYCGI09" target="_self">Sociotechnical Systems: IT and the Future of Work </a><br /><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/current_students/syllabus/compgc/compgc22_software_engineering/" target="_self">Software Engineering</a>*<br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/archaeology/studying/masters/courses/ARCLG117" target="_self">Spatial Statistics, Network Analysis and Human History</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG035" target="_self">Systems Management</a><br /><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/eme/study/modules/unstitching" target="_self">Unstitching the Early Modern: Archival and Book Skills</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/eme/study/modules/web01" target="_self">Web 0.1: Early Modern Information Culture, c.1450-c.1750</a></p>
<p class="p">   *Note that these modules have significant prerequisites; for more details see the module page or the programme <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc/UCLDH_MaMSc_Supplementary2016.pdf" target="_self">supplementary prospectus.</a> </p>
<p class="p">    In addition to those listed above, subject to agreement of the module tutor and Programme Director, one module may be taken from any of those offered in the faculties of:</p>
<ul class="disc">
<li> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/ah" target="_blank">Arts and Humanities</a></li>
<li> <a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/" target="_blank">Computer Science</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/shs" target="_blank">Social and Historical Studies</a></li>
</ul>

<h3 class="heading"></h3>





<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading">Entry requirements</h3>





<p class="p">                  Potential applicants
need to have a first or upper second-class Honours degree in
a relevant Humanities or Computing discipline from a UK university,
or an overseas qualification of an equivalent standard.<br /></p>
<p class="p"> <strong>Please note that we DO NOT accept applications from agencies and we will not communicate with an agent regarding your application. We expect all applicants to complete their applications themselves.</strong></p>
<p class="p">       The <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/life/international" target="_self">English Language Proficiency Requirement</a>
 for all non-native English speakers is<br /></p>
<ul class="disc">
<li>IELTS: a minimum of 7.0 with no less than 6.5 in each sub-set. </li>
<li>TOEFL: a minimum overall score of 100 with 24/30 in reading and writing and 20/30 in speaking and listening.</li>
</ul>
<p class="p"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/clie/graduate-preparation-courses/pre-sessional" target="_blank">Pre-sessional English courses</a>
 are available to introduce students to the UK academic 
culture as well as improving written and spoken English. Attendance on 
these courses does not guarantee that you will be accepted onto the 
programme. <br /></p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading">Fees: 2017-2018 session</h3>








<h5 class="heading">Full-time MA/MSc</h5>



<p class="p">                UK/EU students: £9,290<br />Overseas students: £20,005</p>



<h5 class="heading">         Part time: 2 years</h5>



<p class="p">pro-rata<br /></p>



<h5 class="heading">Flexible (modular): up to 5 years</h5>



<p class="p">       pro-rata depending on the number of credits taken per year.</p>



<h5 class="heading">Diploma and Certificate
</h5>



<p class="p">  details are on the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/current-students/money/2017-2018_fees" target="_self">UCL Fee Schedule: Postgraduate Taught 2017-2018</a></p>
<hr class="rule" />
<p class="p"><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/current-students/money/2016-2017_fees/2016-17_postgrad_taught" target="_blank"></a></p>

<h3 class="heading"></h3>






<h3 class="heading">Funding</h3>





<p class="p">                  For funding details
please visit <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/scholarships" target="_self">Scholarships and Funding</a>.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading"></h3>






<h3 class="heading">How to apply</h3>





<p class="p">                To apply online: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/taught/degrees/digital-humanities-ma-msc" target="_self">Application and entry</a>. <br /></p>
<p class="p"> <strong>Note that UCL admissions will not accept applications after 28th July.</strong></p>
<hr class="rule" />

                        <article class="article clearfix">
                            <!-- Start Silva content --> 
<h1 class="heading">Short Courses in DH</h1>

<h2 class="heading"></h2>





<img src="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/images/tower-boat.png" width="149" height="148" alt="tower boat" class="no-respond float-right" title="tower boat" /><p class="lead"> In addition to the full Master's programme, the following short courses in Digital Humanities are also offered by the department.</p>

<h2 class="heading"></h2>






<h2 class="heading">Certificate in Digital Humanities</h2>





<p class="p"> This is a very flexible programme for anyone looking to extend their skill set, particularly for CPD. Students registered for the Certificate must complete four modules from our DH core and options list as agreed with the Programme Director. The length of time taken depends on the student's circumstances (they may be working full-time or using this programme to complement other studies) and can range from a single term to a maximum of two years.    </p>
<p class="p"> The course unit value is 60 credits or 24 ECTS which are transferable in the UK and EU.<br /></p>
<p class="p"> Application is through the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/taught/degrees/digital-humanities-ma-msc" target="_self">UCL portal</a> and the fees are pro-rata (by credits) depending on those for the full Master's programme. </p>

<h2 class="heading">Diploma in Digital Humanities</h2>





<p class="p"> Again this is a very flexible programme with students taking all five core modules from the full Master's programme and a further three from the optional modules list. Diploma students do not take the workplacement or dissertation modules. This can be completed full-time over nine months or by flexible study over two to five years.</p>
<p class="p"> The course unit value is 120 credits or 48 ECTS which are transferable in the UK and EU. </p>
<p class="p"> Under the current UCL regulations for the Accreditation of Prior Learning (APL) credit transfer, a student who has already completed a PG Diploma and then applies for the Master’s programme will receive APL of 120 credits; this means that students holding a Diploma in DH would only need to complete the Dissertation to receive the full Master's degree. <br /></p>
<p class="p"> Application is through the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/taught/degrees/digital-humanities-ma-msc" target="_self">UCL portal</a> and the fees are pro-rata (by credits) depending on those for the full Master's programme. <br /></p>

<h2 class="heading">Graduate Affiliate Studies</h2>





<p class="p"> If you are currently enrolled at another institution it may be possible for you to study at our department to complement your work. Students usually come for one term and with this <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/international/affiliate/graduate/" target="_self">scheme</a>, although it is not possible to receive a UCL qualification, it is usually possible to count credit taken here towards the degree in the home institution. This would need to be confirmed with the home institution first.  </p>

<h2 class="heading">Individual Short Course modules</h2>





<p class="p">          Many of the modules that are offered by the Department of Information Studies as part of the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc" target="_blank">MA/MSc in Digital Humanities</a> programme work as stand-alone short courses for those wishing to update their professional skills in a particular area.</p>
<p class="p"> The modules are taught over one term, usually for one morning or one afternoon per week with 30 taught hours of lectures and practicals, followed by a coursework assessment or exam (which is optional for short course students). If the assessment is completed successfully, the module credit can count towards a future Master's degree.<br /></p>
<p class="p"> Many of these modules are CILIP accredited and so suitable for CPD for Library and Information professionals.<br /></p>
<p class="p">          DH modules currently offered as Short Courses include:</p>
<p class="p"> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG008" target="_blank">Digital Resources in the Humanities</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG038" target="_blank">Electronic Publishing</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG017" target="_blank">Internet Technologies</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank">Introduction to Programming and Scripting </a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG019" target="_blank">Legal and Social Aspects of Electronic Publishing</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank">Server Programming and Structured Data</a><br /><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank">XML</a></p>
<p class="p"> Acceptance onto the module is by agreement by the tutor.  Many other modules from taught programmes offered by UCL Department of Information Studies (DIS) are available as <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/short-courses-cpd-information-studies" target="_self">short courses</a>. Details about fees and how to apply are also available on that page. <br /></p>



<h4 class="heading"></h4>





<!-- End Silva content -->

                     <div class="content-sidebar">
                                        <div class="site-content__sidebar">

<h3 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc">MA/MSc in DigitalHumanities</a> </h3>





<p class="p"> The <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/short/mamsc">MA/MSc programme</a>, offered via <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis">UCL Department of Information Studies</a>,  is a new interdisciplinary degree exploring the intersection of digital technologies and culture.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/PhD">Doctorates</a> </h3>





<p class="p"> We have a variety of <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/doctorates" target="_self">doctoral students</a>
 who are undertaking research with us, and are interested in hearing 
from those who are considering undertaking PhD research in Digital 
Humanities. </p>

</div>

                    </div>
                </div>
            </div>
        </div>
        <!--noindex-->

                        <article class="article clearfix">
                            <!-- Start Silva content --> 


<h2 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc">MA/MSc in DigitalHumanities</a> </h2>





<p class="p"> The <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/short/mamsc">MA/MSc programme</a>, offered via <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis">UCL Department of Information Studies</a>,  is a new interdisciplinary degree exploring the intersection of digital technologies and culture.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h2 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/PhD">Doctorates</a> </h2>





<p class="p"> We have a variety of <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/doctorates" target="_self">doctoral students</a>
 who are undertaking research with us, and are interested in hearing 
from those who are considering undertaking PhD research in Digital 
Humanities. </p>


<!-- End Silva content --> 

                        </article>

                                        <div class="site-content__sidebar">

<h3 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc">MA/MSc in DigitalHumanities</a> </h3>





<p class="p"> The <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/short/mamsc">MA/MSc programme</a>, offered via <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis">UCL Department of Information Studies</a>,  is a new interdisciplinary degree exploring the intersection of digital technologies and culture.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/PhD">Doctorates</a> </h3>





<p class="p"> We have a variety of <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/doctorates" target="_self">doctoral students</a>
 who are undertaking research with us, and are interested in hearing 
from those who are considering undertaking PhD research in Digital 
Humanities. </p>

                    <div class="site-content__main">

                        <article class="article clearfix">
                            <!-- Start Silva content --> 
<h1 class="heading">MA/MSc in Digital Humanities</h1>
<p class="lead">The Master's degree in
Digital Humanities at UCL draws together teaching from a wide range
of disciplines, to investigate the application of computational
technologies to the arts, humanities, and cultural heritage. </p>
<p class="p"> The MA/MSc in Digital
Humanities is a truly interdisciplinary programme and has strong teaching links with: </p>
<ul class="disc">
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis" target="_self">UCL Department of Information Studies</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.cs.ucl.ac.uk/" target="_self">UCL
Computer Science</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/ah/" target="_self">Arts and Humanities</a></li>
<li> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/shs/" target="_self">Social and Historical
Sciences</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/engineering/" target="_self">Engineering Science</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.bartlett.ucl.ac.uk/index.php" target="_self">Bartlett Faculty of the Built
Environment</a>. </li>
</ul>
<p class="p">       The programme also draws on facilities offered by:</p>
<ul class="disc">
<li> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/library/" target="_self">UCL Library Services</a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/library/special-coll/" target="_self">Special Collections</a></li>
<li><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/museums/" target="_self">UCL Museums
and Collections</a></li>
</ul>
<p class="p">       as well as liaising closely with a variety of
world-class, London based libraries, archives, and museums within the
vicinity of UCL.</p>

<h2 class="heading">About the Programme</h2>





<p class="p">      The MA/MSc provides research-led teaching delivered by leading scholars.</p>
<p class="p">                  In
Term 1 and 2, students take five core modules, plus a further
three from a wide range of options available from various departments and
faculties at UCL. In addition, students write an original <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony/dissertations" target="_blank">dissertation</a> on a topic of their choice in consultation with their supervisor,
and undertake a <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony/workplacements" target="_blank">workplacement</a> at a related institution where they can apply
taught aspects of the programme in Term 3. This allows students who have a
background in the humanities to acquire necessarily skills in digital
technologies, and also makes it possible for those with a technical
background to become informed about scholarly methods in the humanities.</p>

<h2 class="heading">Terms One and Two</h2>





<p class="p"> The following core modules are mandatory for the programme:</p>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG008" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG008" target="_self">Digital Resources in the Humanities</a><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG008" target="_self"></a> </dt>
  <dd><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG008" target="_blank"></a>Introducing a range of
issues involved in the design, creation, management and use of
digital resources in the humanities. 
</dd>
</dl>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG017" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG017" target="_self">Internet
Technologies</a><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG017" target="_self"></a> </dt>
  <dd>Exploring the basic concepts of markup, website structuring and design, and issues involved in generating, evaluating and delivering online content. 
</dd>
</dl>
<p class="p"> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG017" target="_blank"></a></p>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank">Introduction to Programming and Scripting</a> </dt>
  <dd><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank"></a>      Providing an introduction to the key concepts and 
principles of standard procedural computer programming and a brief 
introduction to relational database querying and manipulation.</dd>
</dl>
<p class="p"> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG018" target="_blank"></a></p>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank">Server Programming and Structured Data</a> </dt>
  <dd><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank"></a>Covering approaches to creating database driven 
websites, with a focus on applications relating to maps and spatial 
data. </dd>
</dl>
<p class="p"> <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG033" target="_blank"></a></p>


<h3 class="heading"><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank"></a></h3>




<dl class="dl" compact="compact">
<dt><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/study/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank">XML</a> </dt>
  <dd><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/taught/pg/INSTG037" target="_blank"></a>Providing an overview
of Extensible Markup language; giving students the opportunity to
practice XML markup techniques, processing with XSLT, and demonstrating the use of XML in
publishing.</dd>
</dl>
<p class="p"> Note that the technical core modules are all at entry level; for 
students that already have demonstrable competencies in these areas, it 
may be possible, subject to the agreement of the Programme Director, to 
substitute modules from other UCL departments.</p>
<p class="p"> There are also a wide range of taught <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc/optionalmodules">optional modules</a> that are elective.</p>

<h2 class="heading"> Term Three</h2>





<p class="p"> This is for coursework assignments, exams and the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony/workplacements" target="_blank">Workplacement Module</a> and is followed by the
<a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/simonmahony/dissertations" target="_blank">dissertation</a> (60 credits). 
</p>

<h2 class="heading">Further information</h2>





<ul class="disc">
<li>Some suggestions for <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/courses/mamsc/DHpreliminaryreading.pdf" target="_self">preliminary reading</a>.</li>
</ul>
<ul class="disc">
<li>For background on Digital Humanities see <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dh/events/archive/susanhockey" target="_self">The Susan Hockey Lecture in Digital Humanities </a>(video 63.52 mins)</li>
<li>For international students: <a href="http://www.prepareforsuccess.org.uk/" target="_self">Prepare for success</a> (Learning activities to prepare you for study in the UK)</li>
<li>Term Dates: <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/staff/term-dates/2017-2018" target="_blank">2017-2018</a></li>
<li>Useful information about <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/accommodation" target="_blank">Student Accommodation</a></li>
<li>Information for new students <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/occasional/information-new-students" target="_blank">2017-18</a></li>
</ul>
<p class="p">                  Academic enquiries should go to the Programme Director, <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/juliannenyhan" target="_blank">Julianne Nyhan</a> <br /></p>
<p class="p">                  Admissions enquiries should go to Sarah Davenport (<a href="mailto:s.davenport@ucl.ac.uk" target="_self">s.davenport@ucl.ac.uk</a>) <br /></p>
<p class="p">                  Core teaching staff
include:</p>
<ul class="disc">
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/simon-mahony/" target="_blank">Simon Mahony</a> </li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/infostudies/julianne-nyhan/" target="_blank">Julianne Nyhan </a></li>
<li><a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/dis/people/oliverdukewilliams" target="_blank">Oliver Duke-Williams</a> </li>
</ul>
<p class="p">                    A variety of other
teaching staff from across various departments at UCL will also teach
on the programme, depending on modules chosen.  
</p>


<!-- End Silva content --> 

                        </article>

<h3 class="heading"></h3>





<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading">Entry requirements</h3>





<p class="p">                  Potential applicants
need to have a first or upper second-class Honours degree in
a relevant Humanities or Computing discipline from a UK university,
or an overseas qualification of an equivalent standard.<br /></p>
<p class="p"> <strong>Please note that we DO NOT accept applications from agencies and we will not communicate with an agent regarding your application. We expect all applicants to complete their applications themselves.</strong></p>
<p class="p">       The <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/life/international" target="_self">English Language Proficiency Requirement</a>
 for all non-native English speakers is<br /></p>
<ul class="disc">
<li>IELTS: a minimum of 7.0 with no less than 6.5 in each sub-set. </li>
<li>TOEFL: a minimum overall score of 100 with 24/30 in reading and writing and 20/30 in speaking and listening.</li>
</ul>
<p class="p"> <a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/clie/graduate-preparation-courses/pre-sessional" target="_blank">Pre-sessional English courses</a>
 are available to introduce students to the UK academic 
culture as well as improving written and spoken English. Attendance on 
these courses does not guarantee that you will be accepted onto the 
programme. <br /></p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading">Fees: 2017-2018 session</h3>








<h5 class="heading">Full-time MA/MSc</h5>



<p class="p">                UK/EU students: £9,290<br />Overseas students: £20,005</p>



<h5 class="heading">         Part time: 2 years</h5>



<p class="p">pro-rata<br /></p>



<h5 class="heading">Flexible (modular): up to 5 years</h5>



<p class="p">       pro-rata depending on the number of credits taken per year.</p>



<h5 class="heading">Diploma and Certificate
</h5>



<p class="p">  details are on the <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/current-students/money/2017-2018_fees" target="_self">UCL Fee Schedule: Postgraduate Taught 2017-2018</a></p>
<hr class="rule" />
<p class="p"><a href="https://www.ucl.ac.uk/current-students/money/2016-2017_fees/2016-17_postgrad_taught" target="_blank"></a></p>

<h3 class="heading"></h3>






<h3 class="heading">Funding</h3>





<p class="p">                  For funding details
please visit <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/scholarships" target="_self">Scholarships and Funding</a>.</p>
<hr class="rule" />

<h3 class="heading"></h3>






<h3 class="heading">How to apply</h3>





<p class="p">                To apply online: <a href="http://www.ucl.ac.uk/prospective-students/graduate/taught/degrees/digital-humanities-ma-msc" target="_self">Application and entry</a>. <br /></p>
<p class="p"> <strong>Note that UCL admissions will not accept applications after 28th July.</strong></p>
